Local News

The Entire Board of Directors and Supervisors of China Merchants Bureau Sworn into Office Zhu Jiajie Personally Arrived Yesterday to Give Instructions and Open a Joint Meeting General Manager Liu Hongsheng Arrived at the Bureau Yesterday to Take Up His Duties The Board of Directors of Two Departments Were Temporarily Suspended Yesterday Pending Further Action 70

After the reorganization of China Merchants Bureau was ordered, the board of directors and supervisors was officially established yesterday morning. All the directors and supervisors, as well as General Manager Liu Hongsheng, were sworn into office at 9:00 am yesterday morning in the Central Bank building at No. 2 Jiujiang Road. Minister of Transportation Zhu Jiajie personally arrived to supervise and give instructions. After the inauguration, a joint meeting of the board of directors and supervisors was held immediately. Around 10:00 am, the entire group went to the bureau to take up their duties and receive various files and accounts from the Supervisory Office and the General Manager's Office. Because the results of the board of directors were not yet complete, it will be received again at a fixed time. At noon, Minister Zhu Jiajie hosted a banquet for the directors and supervisors on Fourth Road and met with reporters to formally issue a statement. The Ministry of Transportation will submit the pier loan matter to today's Central Political Committee for discussion. Mr. Sudeer, the general director of the China Business Company, issued a statement regarding the loan matter and made some explanations. Li Guojie is still under supervision. His wife visited him yesterday morning and sent him daily necessities. The details are recorded separately below.

Establishment of the Supervisory Committee 71

Yesterday morning around 9:00 AM, the new General Manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company (CMSNC), Liu Hongsheng, along with Executive Directors Ye Zhuotang, Shi Liangcai, Zhang Shouyong, Zhang Gongquan, Du Yuesheng, Yang Ying, Directors Hu Bijian, Li Fuxun, Wang Xiaolai, Qian Xinzhi, Yu Rizhang (absent), Zhang Xiaolin, Hu Junzhuang, and Sheng Ping, gathered for a photograph marking the establishment of the CMSNC Board of Directors and Supervisors. (Photo by Li Zunyong)

Ministers and Supervisors Lu Xuepu, Chen Guangfu, Yu Qiaqing, Hu Mengjia, Qin Runqing, Rong Zongjing, Huang Jinrong (absent), Guo Shun, etc., held a swearing-in ceremony in the auditorium on the third floor of the Central Bank. Minister of Transportation Zhu Jiahua attended to administer the oath and deliver an address. The meeting was chaired by Minister Zhu, and the agenda was as follows: 1) Paying the highest respect to the portrait of Sun Yat-sen and the national flag; 2) The chairman respectfully reading Sun Yat-sen's will; 3) The directors and supervisors taking the oath; 4) Minister Zhu's address; 5) The directors' and supervisors' representative's response; 6) General Manager Liu's response. The ceremony lasted only half an hour, after which the first joint meeting of the directors and supervisors was held.

Oath of the Directors and Supervisors 72

All directors and supervisors raised their right hands and, led by the oath administrator, Minister of Transportation Zhu Jiahua, took the oath: "I solemnly swear that I will strictly abide by Sun Yat-sen's will, obey party principles, abide by national laws, be loyal and diligent in my duties, and economize on expenses. I will never employ useless personnel, engage in embezzlement, or accept bribes. If I violate this oath, I am willing to accept the most severe punishment from the party."

Minister Zhu's Address 73

After the new directors and supervisors took the oath, Minister Zhu delivered an address, saying, "Distinguished directors and supervisors, General Manager Liu, today's swearing-in ceremony is of great significance for the future of the CMSNC. I have only recently taken over as Minister of Transportation at the beginning of this month, and despite the heavy workload, I have come here specifically for this matter, which concerns our country's shipping industry, to discuss future development plans with you all. The CMSNC is our country's only shipping enterprise of considerable scale. Since its establishment in the eleventh year of Tongzhi (1872), it has developed thanks to government funding. However, after being transferred to commercial management, due to the control of a few individuals, its business has declined, and malpractices have become rampant, worsening year by year, day by day. After the eleventh year of the Republic (1922), interest payments were suspended, and its credit was ruined. The company's problems should have been addressed more than a decade ago. The reason for the delay is that the government still trusts commercially-run enterprises and believes that shareholders should handle and rectify the situation themselves. In addition, the adverse domestic political environment in recent years has meant that the central government has been focused on unification efforts and dealing with military and political issues, without being able to attend to this. Therefore, although the CMSNC has decayed to the extreme, the government has only adopted a supervisory policy, hoping that under strict government supervision, its business could be improved and stabilized, and then further developed. However, the supervisory system has been in place for five years now, and not only has it achieved nothing, but the company's business has collapsed like a raging tide, beyond salvation. Thinking of this, it is truly heartbreaking. The company's current debt has reached over 17.9 million yuan. One set of shares (i.e., two shipping shares and one property share) had a nominal value of 100 taels and 100 yuan, totaling 270-280 taels. Although they are now said to be worth 30 taels, in reality, no one on the market is interested in these shares anymore, except for a few people who use them for speculative trading. The true value of CMSNC shares is virtually zero. Although it is said to have 25 ships,

many of them are over half a century old, and some are over 20 or 30 years old. Such old and dilapidated ships are no longer suitable for use. All the warehouses and docks are also in disrepair and severely damaged. In the midst of this dilapidated situation, the company's business is on the verge of collapse, and the hope for its self-rescue has been completely extinguished. The central government believes that the company's business is related to national maritime policy and the national economy, so it has decisively decided to take it back into state ownership. In consideration of the shareholders' investment, the government will buy back the shares at 50 taels per set, based on the average market price of 30 taels, 6 mace, and 6 candareens over the past three years. In the midst of the country's financial difficulties, increasing this burden is a last resort, especially during this time of national crisis, when raising this large sum is even more difficult. The central government, prioritizing the national industry and commerce and the people's livelihood, has made this sacrifice with determination. Many state-owned enterprises in various countries incur losses, especially in the shipping industry. However, some countries still adopt state-owned policies, in order to subsidize industry and commerce and maintain the country's shipping position. Because of these special circumstances, they do not hesitate to make sacrifices. Now, the central government's adoption of the state-owned system for the CMSNC is prepared to make sacrifices in order to break the deadlock, recover rights and interests, endure the pain for a while, seek future benefits, save the crisis today, and establish a grand plan for a hundred years. In order to gather ideas and benefit from diverse perspectives, the government has appointed prominent figures from the industrial and commercial sectors to form a board of directors and supervisors, actively proceed, and jointly seek the development of China's shipping industry. You all have achieved excellent results in the industrial and commercial sectors and have a long-standing history in your respective localities. You will surely be able to unite and work hard with a spirit of great fearlessness and sacrifice, abide by your oaths, and strive for the progress of the company's affairs. The future of the nation truly depends on it."

Response from the Directors and Supervisors 74

Shi Liangcai, representing the board of directors and supervisors, delivered a response, saying, "Liangcai and others have been appointed as directors and supervisors of the CMSNC and are taking office today. We appreciate Minister Zhu's instructions. We believe that the board of directors is the body responsible for managing the company's affairs, and the board of supervisors is the body responsible for overseeing the company's affairs. Both have extremely important responsibilities. Liangcai and others will abide by Minister Zhu's instructions, jointly take responsibility, and reorganize the company's affairs in order to live up to the government's intentions to improve the shipping industry."

Response from the General Manager 75

General Manager Liu Hongsheng delivered a response, saying, "I, Hongsheng, have been appointed by the National Government as a director and general manager of the CMSNC. I humbly believe that I am not qualified to take on this important task. However, the CMSNC is our country's only shipping organization, with a history of over 60 years. It is currently riddled with problems and in urgent need of reorganization. I have no choice but to reluctantly take on this difficult task. Today, I am taking office in accordance with the order, and I will follow Minister Zhu's instructions. I will also abide by the instructions of the board of directors, diligently and cautiously handle matters, and strive to live up to the government's intentions to reorganize the shipping industry."

Meeting of the Directors and Supervisors 76

After the directors and supervisors took the oath of office, they immediately held the first joint meeting of the directors and supervisors at 9:50 AM. All directors and supervisors were present, as well as General Manager Liu Hongsheng. Minister of Transportation Zhu Jiahua and Director of the Shipping Administration Department Gao Tingzi attended as observers. After Chairman Shi Liangcai reported, the discussion began immediately, focusing on: 1) the provisional articles of association of the CMSNC; 2) the provisional articles of association of the CMSNC board of supervisors; and 3) the provisional articles of association of the CMSNC board of directors. The wording was revised and passed, and the meeting adjourned at 10:10 AM. The entire group then went to the CMSNC to take over.

Situation During the Taking Over 77

After the joint meeting of the directors and supervisors adjourned, General Manager Liu Hongsheng, accompanied by Minister Zhu, Director Gao of the Shipping Administration Department, and the directors and supervisors, went to the company to take over. The entire staff of the CMSNC had been assigned to appoint Zhu Zhilin and others to serve as receptionists, and Chinese and Western detectives were temporarily deployed for special security. After arriving at the company, they rested in the General Manager's office and received congratulations from Fu Zongyao, Xu Jiying, Chen Songyuan, Chen Zheqing, Hu Junqiu, Hu Junzhuang, Man Yanfang, Chen Bogang, Chen Xing, and others. Around 11:00 AM, all the directors and supervisors and the general manager took a group photo in the auditorium.

Recent Photo of Liu Hongsheng (Zhonghua Press)

Address to the Staff 78

At 11:30 AM, the entire staff gathered in the main auditorium, where General Manager Liu Hongsheng and Executive Director Shi Liangcai gave speeches. Liu said, "Although the CMSNC is now state-owned, it was originally a commercial organization. Now that I am serving as General Manager, from now on, all matters of the company must focus on commercialization in order to gradually improve. Regarding the employment of personnel, we must consider both talent and economy as principles. I hope that those who have achieved results in the past will work together with us. This is extremely fortunate." Shi said, "The CMSNC has a long history. This time, we have come with a spirit of sacrifice, without any desire for personal gain. I hope that everyone will work hard and encourage each other to restore the CMSNC to its original position."

Taking Over of Various Departments 79

At 11:45 AM, Directors Shi Liangcai, Ye Zhuotang, and Hu Junzhuang, accompanied by Gao Tingzi, Director of the Shipping Administration Department of the Ministry of Transportation, and Qi Fuming and Xu Zhiyi of the Secretariat, went to the Supervisory Office to take over. The handover was carried out by Zeng Huiwen, the secretary designated by the former supervisor, Chen Fumu. From 1:00 PM, the General Affairs Department was taken over by the newly appointed Chen Weiqing, the Accounting Department by the newly appointed Director Xu Guangde, the Business Department by the newly appointed Director He Molin, the Shipping Department by the newly appointed Director Zhao Yun, and the Property Department by Xu Zhiyi of the Secretariat. The takeover was completed last night. However, the board of directors was originally scheduled to be taken over by the board of directors, but because the chairman of the board, Li Guojie, did not notify them in advance to complete the process, the board of directors temporarily postponed the takeover and will take over after the process is completed.

Appointment of New Staff 80

After the new General Manager took office, the old staff members submitted their resignations. Yesterday, a special order was issued to appoint Chen Weiqing as the Director of the General Affairs Department, Xu Guangde as the Director of the Accounting Department, He Molin as the Director of the Business Department, Chen Da as the Director of the Department, Zhao Yun as the Director of the Shipping Department, and Xu Zhiyi and Qi Fuming as staff members of the Secretariat.

Reporting the Takeover 81

After Liu and others took over, they telegraphed the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Transportation in the afternoon to report the takeover and the process. The original telegram from the newly appointed General Manager Liu Hongsheng read, "To Song, Acting President of the Executive Yuan, and Zhu, Minister of Transportation: I, Hongsheng, have been appointed as the General Manager of the CMSNC and have taken over today together with the directors and supervisors. In addition to submitting a separate report on the takeover, I respectfully submit this telegram. Liu Hongsheng, General Manager of the CMSNC, respectfully." The telegram from the entire board of directors and supervisors read, "To Song, Acting President of the Executive Yuan, and Zhu and Yu, Vice Ministers of Transportation: We, Zhuotang and others, have been appointed as directors and supervisors of the CMSNC and have taken office today. We immediately held a joint meeting of the directors and supervisors and held the first meeting of the directors and supervisors. In addition to taking over with the General Manager, we respectfully submit this telegram. The CMSNC Board of Directors and Supervisors respectfully."

Zhu Jiahua's Remarks 82

After hosting a banquet for the directors and supervisors and General Manager Liu at Xinghualou yesterday at noon, Minister of Transportation Zhu Jiahua spoke with reporters from various newspapers at 3:00 PM, discussing the reorganization of the CMSNC and the reasons for monitoring Li Guojie, as follows: 1)

I came to Shanghai yesterday for the CMSNC matter and discussed the post-reorganization matters with the directors and supervisors and General Manager Liu. 2) The loan agreement signed by the CMSNC with foreign businesses this time was not submitted to the ministry for approval in advance. Even the various sectors in Shanghai were unaware of it. Therefore, after the Ministry of Transportation received the news, it telegraphed Li Guojie, asking him to send all the contracts and memoranda to the ministry for review. Li Guojie sent them on the 12th. After reviewing them, the contents were intricate and complex, and a detailed study is required to determine how to proceed. Now that the directors and supervisors and the General Manager have taken office, they should collect all the documents related to this case and then review and discuss the solutions. 3) Li Guojie also deeply regrets his mistakes this time and has voluntarily reported them. The government believes that the matter is of great importance, so it is temporarily monitoring him in order to easily clear up this case. 4) The major contract signed this time has not been approved by the ministry, so it will naturally not be recognized. 5) The loan has not yet been implemented, and whether the foreign businesses have paid a small portion of the cash needs to be clarified after a thorough investigation." When reporters from Xinsheng News Agency and others raised various questions, Zhu responded as follows: (Q) After Li Guojie is monitored, what will be done? (A) Li is currently being monitored at the home of a friend in the Chinese-controlled area. Except for not being able to go out, everything else is very free. Although this loan has not been implemented, Li's name is signed on the draft. Whether the Supervisory Office has indeed allowed Li to handle it needs to be investigated on documents other than the contract. However, the Supervisory Office is under the jurisdiction of the Ministry of Transportation, and Chen Fumu did not submit it to the ministry for approval. Therefore, not only is it not legal, but the case is extremely complicated. To avoid the expansion of the incident, Li Guojie is temporarily monitored. The handling of the matter will be decided after the entire contract issue is reviewed and studied. (Q) This time, four warehouses are pledged or rumored, but Li's statement refers to three warehouses. How many warehouses are there? (A) According to the contract and attachments sent to the ministry by Li Guojie on the 12th, there are four warehouses. However, because the contract is in Chinese and English, it still needs to be compared to see if they match. (Q) What is Chen Fumu's responsibility? (A) Of course, it needs to be studied. Monitoring Li Guojie is also for this purpose, but before a formal determination is made, I cannot answer. However, it is clear that the CMSNC borrowed a huge amount of 30 million in foreign debt this time without submitting it to the ministry for approval and keeping it secret, which does not comply with legal procedures. Even other businesses must report to the government for approval if they borrow tens of millions in foreign debt. (Q) What is the loss of this loan? (A) Absorbing foreign investment is originally one of the methods, but it depends on whether the rights belong to us or to the other party. The degree of conflict between this CMSNC loan and national rights is not fully known, but in terms of the construction loan, the plan is to build a large building on more than 20 acres along Sichuan Road outside Fuzhou Road. In addition to self-use, the remaining part is leased, and it is estimated that it can be repaid in 15 years, but the contract stipulates 20 years, and the right to manage the lease is in the hands of the other party, and a handling fee must be paid. Isn't it the case that at least five years' rent has been handed over to others? As for the dock loan and the ship purchase loan, they are ostensibly Sino-foreign joint operations, but in fact, the rights are in the hands of the other party, and the losses will be even greater. (Q) Is the return to state ownership due to the loan issue? (A) The motivation for returning to state ownership was unrelated to the discovery of the loan. Li cited the reasons for returning to state ownership and reorganizing the company as the fact that the CMSNC's business was extremely developed during the state-owned period, and the purchase of land gradually increased to 40 million in assets, all during this period. Since it was changed to commercial operation, it has become worse and worse, gradually entering a crisis, and it is controlled by a few people, with heavy debts and no way to reorganize it. This is a larger shipping organization in our country, and it has a great relationship with industry and commerce, so the government has decided to take it back into state ownership after several considerations. (Q) It is said that some millions of yuan have been withdrawn in advance in this loan. Has the minister heard of it? (A) It has not been found yet, but this case is definitely not that simple. (Q) What are the new plans after returning to state ownership? (A) First, eliminate the malpractices, and then set new plans. (Q) Will the government allocate funds for reorganization? (A) Of course, the government will treat state ownership the same as other state-owned enterprises, and allocate some funds first as working capital. (Q) What will happen to the shares of the Jiyu Company? (A) The shares of the Jiyu Company and the shipping shares are actually one. Therefore, the CMSNC shares are traded as a set, with a total of 8 million yuan, of which 4 million yuan are Jiyu Company shares and 4 million yuan are shipping shares. (Q) When will the repurchase of commercial shares be implemented? Is it possible for those who have shares to have no objection to the evaluation of 36 taels? (A) The repurchase of commercial shares will be implemented soon. The evaluation of 36 taels was not only discussed jointly with the business community before it was determined, but also evaluated by the exchange after combining the market prices of the three years of the Republic of China 19, 20, and 21. In fact, it is very fair. Moreover, the CMSNC has not only accumulated debts of 17 million taels in recent years, but also has not paid interest since the 11th year. Although there is still a price on the market, it is just a speculative effect, and the essence is equal to zero. In short, whether the shares are valuable or not depends on whether the interest is paid. Since the market situation in the past three years has been evaluated, it cannot be said to be unfair. (Q) What if some shareholders do not want the government to buy back the shares? (A) This matter will be studied again, and there will probably be no problem. Finally, (Q) What is the current situation of the resignation of the Director of the Postal Service? (A) I have sent a letter to Director Huang (Nai Shu) to Beijing to discuss it in order to retain him. Zhu said that after the matter was completed, he would return to Beijing on the overnight express train.

Liu Hongsheng's Remarks 83

After taking office, General Manager Liu made the following remarks to reporters: "I, having had my humble talents erroneously selected by the National Government and appointed as a Director and General Manager of the CMSNC, ask myself if my limited abilities are truly adequate for this heavy responsibility. However, this matter relates to our nation’s shipping industry, and is of utmost importance. I cannot but strive to exhaust my meager strength. This reorganization involves making this Bureau State-owned, differing in nature from the past. In the future, major policies and all important plans regarding this Bureau will be under the authority of the Ministry of Transportation. The General Manager’s responsibility lies only in faithfully executing the plans and intentions set by the Ministry and the Board of Directors. I shall exert all my meager abilities and diligently devote myself to the task, striving to live up to the Government’s intention to develop the shipping industry. If I am fortunate enough to receive unbiased guidance and unanimous assistance from all sectors, it would not only be my personal fortune."

Reporting the Dock Pledge 84

Li Guojie, the former General Manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, borrowed money from the China General Commercial Company and the Dalae Steamship Company, pledging the docks for: 1) Construction loans, 2) Dock loans, and 3) Purchasing new ships on credit, totaling 30 million yuan. After the China General Commercial Company took over the dock loan case, Hong Dezhao, the Deputy Director of the Dock Affairs Department, went to the CMSNC yesterday afternoon to report the progress to the new General Manager, Liu Hongsheng. At 4:00 PM, the China General Commercial Company sent personnel to the CMSNC to explain the pledge process to Liu Hongsheng.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Organization 85

Provisional Articles of Association of the CMSNC, Article 1: This Bureau is a State-owned enterprise, directly under the Ministry of Transportation. Article

Page 14

2: This Bureau shall have one General Manager, appointed by the Ministry of Transportation upon request, to execute the Bureau’s affairs. Article 3: Under the General Manager, there shall be one to three Secretaries, appointed by the General Manager, to manage all confidential documents and other matters. Article 4: This Bureau, as necessary to inspect the businesses of the various sub-bureaus and ships, may appoint two Inspectors, appointed by the General Manager. Article 5: This Bureau shall have the following departments, each with one Director and several staff members, all appointed by the General Manager. Each department, depending on the complexity of the business, may appoint one Deputy Director, appointed by the General Manager. 1. General Affairs Department, 2. Business Department, 3. Shipping Department, 4. Dock Affairs Department, 5. Accounting Department, 6. Property Department. Article 6: The responsibilities of the General Affairs Department are as follows: 1. Regarding the safekeeping of all important documents and seals; 2. Regarding the receipt and dispatch of documents; 3. Regarding the drafting of various Chinese and foreign documents; 4. Regarding the registration, transfer, and safekeeping of shares; 5. Regarding international publicity and translation; 6. Regarding statistics and investigation; 7. Regarding Party affairs, school affairs, and union affairs; 8. Regarding meeting records; 9. Regarding the acquisition, dispatch, and safekeeping of materials; 10. Regarding personnel registration and staff recruitment, promotion, security, and attendance; 11. Regarding general affairs, health management, and equipment; 12. Regarding the promulgation and notification of all laws and regulations, and the reporting of business conditions; 13. Regarding the safekeeping and registration of files; 14. Regarding the review of free and half-price ship tickets; 15. Regarding matters not belonging to other departments. Article 7: The occupations of the Business Department are as follows: 1. Regarding the allocation, dispatch, and planning of ships on various routes; 2. Regarding the investigation and reporting of domestic and foreign shipping businesses; 3. Regarding the scheduling of ships; 4. Regarding the solicitation and clearing of passengers and goods; 5. Regarding the determination of freight rates; 6. Regarding the determination of passenger ticket rates; 7. Regarding the determination of passenger commission rates; 8. Regarding the review of various handling fees; 9. Regarding contact with customs; 10. Regarding the calculation of shipping costs; 11. Regarding the performance evaluation of the business directors of each ship; 12. Regarding the performance evaluation of each sub-bureau office; 13. Regarding contact with the industry; 14. Regarding the filling and issuing of free and half-price ship tickets; 15. Regarding the management of inland shipping businesses; 16. Regarding the chartering of ships. Article 8: The responsibilities of the Shipping Department are as follows: 1. Regarding the management of ship pilots, mechanics, and their job assignments; 2. Regarding the hiring, firing, and registration of crew members; 3. Regarding the inspection of ship hulls and machinery; 4. Regarding the construction, repair, supervision, and acceptance of ships; 5. Regarding ship equipment and hygiene; 6. Regarding the management and performance evaluation of ship captains and crew members; 7. Regarding the construction, repair, supervision, and acceptance of docks and ships; 8. Regarding bidding for various shipping projects and acceptance; 9. Regarding the drafting of maps for various bureaus, docks, ships, and piers; 10. Regarding the management of ship radio and the performance evaluation of its personnel; 11. Regarding the review of coal and materials used by ships; 12. Regarding ship fire prevention and rescue; 13. Regarding ship insurance; 14. Regarding the management of machine factories and ships. Article 9: The responsibilities of the Dock Affairs Department are: 1. Regarding the solicitation, safekeeping, and storage of goods; 2. Regarding the clearing of goods; 3. Regarding the collection of income from warehouses and docks; 4. Regarding the repair and inspection of warehouses; 5. Regarding warehouse insurance; 6. Regarding warehouse fire prevention and other equipment; 7. Regarding the determination of warehouse rental rates; 8. Regarding the determination of handling rates; 9. Regarding the management, performance evaluation, and job assignment of dock workers; 10. Regarding the supervision and reorganization of dock affairs in various locations; 11. Regarding the management of pier inspectors; 12. Regarding all matters related to coal docks; 13. Regarding the improvement and repair of warehouses, docks, and ships. Article 10: The responsibilities of the Accounting Department are as follows: 1. Regarding the receipt and expenditure of cash; 2. Regarding the safekeeping of bank accounts, books, and checks; 3. Regarding the preparation of budgets and final accounts; 4. Regarding the preparation of balance sheets, income statements, and property catalogs; 5. Regarding the preparation of daily, monthly, and other settlement reports; 6. Regarding the registration, safekeeping, organization, inspection, verification, and accounting of various account books; 7. Regarding the verification of daily notes and vouchers; 8. Regarding the issuance of dividends on shares; 9. Regarding the setting and inspection of accounting for various bureaus, offices, and ships; 10. Regarding the clearing of mortgage loans and other creditor and debtor matters. Article 11: The responsibilities of the Property Department are as follows: 1. Regarding all matters related to the Jiyu Property Company; 2. Regarding the management of various properties; 3. Regarding the investigation and reorganization of properties; 4. Regarding the registration and mapping of properties; 5. Regarding the leasing of properties; 6. Regarding the insurance of properties and the construction of warehouses and docks; 7. Regarding the repair and acceptance of properties; 8. Regarding the payment of taxes and grains on properties; 9. Regarding the design and valuation of properties; 10. Regarding the mapping and surveying of properties; 11. Regarding the consolidation of property mortgages; 12. Regarding the handling of property disputes. Article 12: The articles of association for the various sub-bureaus or offices of this Bureau, and the Jiyu Property Company and the Inland River Steamship Company, shall be formulated separately. Article 13: This Bureau shall establish an Engineering Office, with one Chief Engineer, one Ship Engineer, and one Civil Engineer, and several staff members, who shall, under the command of the General Manager, be responsible for the design, valuation, and verification of various projects. Article 14: All important matters of this Bureau, and the appointment of Secretaries, Directors, and Inspectors, shall be submitted to the Ministry of Transportation for approval. Article 15: This Bureau may employ clerks and trainees in its various departments and offices. Article 16: Matters involving more than two departments shall be handled jointly by the relevant departments. Article 17: Each department of this Bureau may divide its work into sections, and detailed rules shall be formulated separately. Article 18: These articles of association shall come into effect from the date of promulgation and shall be repealed on the date when the formal articles of association are promulgated and approved by the Executive Yuan.

Regulations of the Board of Supervisors 86

Provisional Regulations of the Board of Supervisors of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company: "Article 1" A Board of Supervisors shall be established in the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, directly under the Ministry of Communications; "Article 2" The Board of Supervisors, under the command of the Ministry of Communications, shall supervise all personnel and all business of the entire company; "Article 3" The Board of Supervisors shall consist of nine to thirteen supervisors, appointed by the Minister of Communications; "Article 4" The Board of Supervisors shall have one Chairman of the Board, elected by the supervisors from among themselves to preside over the meetings of the Board of Supervisors and to convene such meetings; "Article 5" The Board of Supervisors shall have one secretary and two clerks; "Article 6" The duties of the Board of Supervisors shall be as follows: (1) To investigate and report on any illegal or derelict conduct by the company's staff; (2) To review important contracts and new borrowing matters; (3) To review budget and final accounts; (4) To inspect accounts and business operations; (5) To supervise other business matters; "Article 7" In addition to the powers prescribed in the preceding article, the Board of Supervisors may, when it deems it beneficial to the company's affairs, put forward opinions to the Board of Directors for their consideration and adoption; "Article 8" The Board of Supervisors may, when it deems it necessary, request the Board of Directors to report or inspect its documents on matters handled by the Board, departments, and offices; "Article 9" The Board of Supervisors may request the Board of Directors to revoke or correct any matter of the company that it deems dangerous or inappropriate; "Article 10" If a dispute arises between the Board of Supervisors and the Board of Directors in the exercise of their powers, the matter may be submitted to the Ministry of Communications for resolution; "Article 11" These Regulations shall come into effect from the date of promulgation and shall be repealed on the date when the formal Regulations are submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval.

Regulations of the Board of Directors 87

Provisional Regulations of the Board of Directors of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company: Article 1 The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company shall establish a Board of Directors directly under the Ministry of Communications. Article 2 The Board of Directors, under the command of the Minister of Communications, shall be in charge of important matters of the entire company and shall be subject to the supervision of the Board of Supervisors. Article 3 The functions and powers of the Board of Directors are as follows: 1. Matters relating to the determination of business policies; 2. Matters relating to the conclusion, repeal, and revision of contracts; 3. Matters relating to the consolidation of property and capital; 4. Matters relating to the review and promulgation of the rules and regulations of the head office and affiliated organizations; 5. Matters relating to the appointment, dismissal, and approval of important personnel below the General Manager; 6. Matters relating to the clearing and repayment of debts and claims; 7. Matters relating to the preparation of budgets; 8. Matters relating to the audit of final accounts; 9. Matters relating to the auditing of business; 10. Matters relating to surplus companies and inland river shipping companies; 11. Matters relating to the planning of other important businesses. Article 4 The Board of Directors shall consist of fifteen to nineteen directors, of which seven shall be managing directors, all of whom shall be selected and appointed by the Ministry of Communications. Article 5 The managing directors shall hold meetings regularly to handle daily affairs. Article 6 Documents of the Board of Directors shall be signed by the managing directors. Article 7 The Board of Directors shall meet once a week. If important matters arise, meetings may be convened at any time by the managing directors. Article 8 Resolutions of the Board of Directors shall be passed by a majority vote of more than half of all directors present, with a quorum of more than half of all directors. Article 9 The chairman of the Board of Directors meetings shall be rotated among the managing directors. Article 10 Important matters of the Board of Directors shall be submitted to the Ministry of Communications for record at any time. Article 11 The Board of Directors shall have one or two secretaries and two to four clerks, who shall be selected by the managing directors and submitted to the Board of Directors for approval and appointment. Article 12 The Board of Directors may employ employees for drafting official documents. Article 13 The expenses of the Board of Directors shall be budgeted by the Board of Directors and submitted to the Ministry of Communications for handling in accordance with the law. Article 14 The rules of procedure for the Board of Directors shall be determined by the Board itself. Article 15 These regulations shall come into effect from the date of promulgation and shall be repealed on the date when the formal regulations are submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval and implementation.

Mr. Suter's Statement 88

Mr. Suter, Director-General of the China General Edison Company, spoke to visitors yesterday regarding the loan to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, stating that the contract signed between the company and the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company was purely commercial in nature and was the result of three years of negotiations between the two parties. All consultations were handled by the Chairman of the Board of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, acting on behalf of the successive supervisors of the Ministry of Communications. Furthermore, as it is a purely commercial contract, both parties will benefit from it, and the future result will not only be to reorganize the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company but also to give it a solid financial foundation and place it in the position of a leading shipping company in the Far East. As for the contents of the contract, due to its commercial confidential nature, he is not yet able to disclose them. What he can state is that among the two contracting parties, his company is the only foreign company, and no other companies have participated.

Submitted to the Central Political Council 89

A telegram from the Ministry of Communications in Beijing states that although the government will inherit all debts of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company when it is converted to state ownership, the nature of these debts must be carefully examined to determine whether they are legal and whether there is any fraud. This matter must be jointly reviewed by the newly established Board of Directors and Board of Supervisors before a decision can be made. As for the matter of Li Guojie's unauthorized mortgage of the company's four warehouses for a large sum of money, which has a significant impact on sovereignty, how the government will deal with this will be submitted to the Executive Yuan meeting on the 15th for discussion to determine specific measures. According to central news, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company case will be submitted to the Central Political Council for discussion on the 16th. Zhu Jiahua has prepared a detailed report on this matter for presentation to the conference.

Labor Union Petitions Yesterday 90

The union of workers at the five wharves of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, including all directors Yu Xianting, Xue Yinkui, Zhang Guiqing, etc., and all group leaders Wang Xinglin, Lin Sheng, etc., totaling more than 70 people, went to the head office yesterday morning at 10:00 to petition for: (1) Opposition to the mortgage of the wharves and a request to ensure the livelihood of the workers; (2) Urging the payment of outstanding wages for October. It happened to be the day the General Manager took office. By 12:00 noon, they met with General Manager Liu Hongsheng, who expressed his hope that the wharf workers would cooperate and work hard to achieve commercialization, and that the livelihood of the workers would naturally be taken into consideration. He ordered the accounting department to raise funds and find a way to pay the outstanding wages.

Situation of the Old Board of Directors 91

Although the new directors and supervisors went to inspect and negotiate with the Board of Directors of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company yesterday, the handover has not yet taken place. According to the person in charge of the Board, Chairman Li has not ordered the completion of the handover. Therefore, when the new directors and supervisors came to the meeting, they were told that they were not prepared and could not hand over. The new directors and supervisors then instructed the existing staff to continue to take full responsibility. As for the surveillance of Chairman Li and the national government's purchase of shares, no opinions could be expressed in this tense situation. In fact, the shareholders' meeting has not been re-elected for more than ten years. Apart from Li Guojie's replacement of the original Chairman Sun Baoqi after he left office, the remaining directors have left office for various reasons. The only person actually responsible now is Mr. Li. As for the various files, they are all here and can be handed over at any time on the order of Chairman Li, according to the Central News Agency.

After Li Guojie was placed under surveillance the day before yesterday, his family went to the Public Security Bureau to inquire about the news. Director Wen of the Bureau told them that Mr. Li was currently confined to his residence and that he was not deprived of any freedom. Mr. Zhu told them that there would be no problem once the case was clarified and that he was only being temporarily guarded due to his responsibilities. It has been notified to Li Jingmei and other members of the Li family to find ways to persuade the authorities, hoping to restore his freedom as soon as possible, according to the New Voice News Agency.

Interview with Zeng Zhongming, Vice Minister of Railways 94

The Third Plenary Session Will Not Discuss the Position of Premier of the Executive Yuan

The Longhai Railway Will Be Completed by Transferring Profits from the Zhengtai Railway

The Claims of the Sino-British Bank Will Not Be a Problem

Zeng Zhongming, Vice Minister of the Ministry of Railways, came to Shanghai the day before yesterday regarding the relocation of the North Railway Station of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway. A reporter from the New Voice News Agency paid him a special visit. Mr. Zeng admitted that the Third Plenary Session would not discuss the position of Premier of the Executive Yuan, and that Wang Jingwei's reinstatement should not be a problem because he had not continued to resign. He also discussed the completion of the Longhai Railway and the claims of the Sino-British Bank. The details are as follows:

Wang's Telegram Will Arrive in the Red Sea 95

Mr. Zeng said that as for the issue of the Premier of the Executive Yuan at the Third Plenary Session, all the important people have agreed that the Central Government should not make any changes. Therefore, the Third Plenary Session will not propose a discussion on this issue. Wang Jingwei has not expressed any further intention to resign since the Central Government approved his request for a three-month extension of his leave. Therefore, his reinstatement should not be a problem. I recently received a telegram informing me that Mr. Wang arrived in Colombo on the 9th of this month and is expected to arrive in the Red Sea on the 17th of this month. I have not heard of him going to Geneva. If he recovers after the three-month leave, he can return to the country.

Longhai and Yuehan Railways 96

Regarding the issue of completing the uncompleted railway loans for the Longhai and Yuehan Railways, Mr. Zeng said that the section of the Yuehan Railway between Shaoguan and Zhuzhou is borrowing 2.45 million pounds from the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Fund. The Standing Committee of the Fund will hold a meeting tomorrow or the day after tomorrow to discuss this. (Note: It has been scheduled for the 17th.) The section of the Longhai Railway between Tongguan and Lanzhou will not issue public bonds. It is planned to transfer the profits from the Zhengtai Railway to complete the railway. Although the amount of this money is not exactly known, it is estimated to be about 12 million yuan. At the same time, another 570,000 pounds will be borrowed from the Boxer Indemnity Fund for the purchase of materials. As for the 60 million yuan loan from France, it is currently shelved and has not been mentioned, so there has been no progress.

Sino-British Company's Claim 97

A reporter from the New Voice News Agency then inquired about the Sino-British Bank's claim of 12.8 million yuan from the Ministry of Railways. Mr. Zeng replied that this matter was a misunderstanding by the Sino-British Bank, which suspected that the Ministry of Railways would sell the site after the North Railway Station was relocated. The Ministry of Railways has now sent Chen Yaozu, Director of the Finance Department, to meet with the company. The result is not yet known, but it should not be a problem.

Zhu Jiahua Telegraphs Huang Naishu to Go to Beijing to Discuss Postal Matters 98

Huang Naishu, Director-General of the Post Office, has repeatedly requested the Ministry of Communications to approve his resignation. Although the Ministry has repeatedly issued orders to retain him, Director Huang is determined to resign and has gone to Hangzhou for recuperation and has not yet returned to Shanghai. It is now learned that the newly appointed Minister of Communications, Zhu Jiahua, telegraphed Hangzhou yesterday, urging Mr. Huang to go to Beijing within a day or two to personally retain him and discuss the improvement of postal services.

Ministry of Industry Sends Personnel to Shanghai to Convene Meeting to Prepare for Acid Plant 99

The Ministry of Industry has recently been actively preparing to establish various machine plants and chemical plants. In addition to preparing to establish copper and iron plants and machine plants, it has recently established a calcium chlorate plant. Minister Chen Gongbo has appointed Liu Yinfu, Director of the Industry Department, and Xu Shanxiang, Technical Supervisor, to handle the matter. After receiving the order, Director Liu came to Shanghai yesterday to convene a preparatory meeting at the International Trade Bureau to discuss the progress of the plant.

Nanjing Road Citizens' Association Advises the Telephone Company

Do Not Use the Means of Cutting Lines to Maintain Social Stability 100

The Nanjing Road Merchants' Association and the District One Citizens' Association of this port, because several shops on Nanjing Road had their telephone lines cut off by the telephone company on the 13th of this month, have sent another letter to the Chinese Ratepayers' Association and the Citizens' General Association, etc., requesting assistance and directly sent a letter to the Shanghai Telephone Company, the original text of which reads: "To whom it may concern: Recently, we have received reports from our members, namely the users of your company, Samsung Factory No. 94834, Hefeng Company No. 94944, Wang Changtai No. 94798, Maoshenghe No. 94717, Changfeng No. 94683, etc., that the telephone fees of these numbers have either been paid for both autumn and winter seasons at the old price, or have not been paid while awaiting the resolution of the price increase negotiations, and all had their lines cut off by your company on November 13, making them unusable. Please help us to argue on their behalf. According to this, our association, as the representative of the majority of members, advocates that the telephone price should not be increased drastically. We have listed the reasons and sent them to your company for your reference. We have recently learned that your company completely disregards the fact that transportation services cannot arbitrarily increase prices or be suspended, and even fails to consider whether the social economy can bear it. It has actually used this kind of decisive means that is not humane, which will inevitably arouse the resentment of the majority of users and create new incidents that cannot be reversed. We believe that your company should not do this. Also, if a theft or fire occurs during this period for the users whose lines have been cut off, and the loss is unlimited due to the inability to use the telephone, who is responsible for creating a state of social unrest? Our association, as the representative body of citizens and merchants, dares to offer a sincere advice again, hoping that you will consider it carefully and immediately restore the right to use the telephone for the users whose lines have been cut off, and stop implementing this method, so as to avoid increasingly serious disputes and maintain public friendship."

Muslims Welcome Representatives from North China 101

The National News Agency reports the following news about Muslim groups yesterday:

Welcoming Representatives from North China 102

The Shanghai Shihui Muslim Research Society convened a general meeting at the Qingzhen Temple on Fuyou Road at 12:00 noon yesterday to welcome the North China Muslim Religious Protection Delegation. The delegates Tang Kesan, Sun Chunwu, Wang Ziqing, Liu Boshi, Wang Mengyang, and Ma Ziwen arrived. More than 100 people, including Ha Shaofu, Da Pusheng, Ha Decheng, Jin Xusheng, Wang Yi, Ma Dawu, Wu Yongxia, Shi Zifan, and Wang Zhizhong, gathered together, making for a grand occasion. Ma Gansheng delivered a welcoming speech, and Wang Ziqing gave a reply, hoping that those with two lings (a transliteration of a Hui word meaning knowledge) would work hard to promote religious teachings, and that a boat of Muslims (i.e., Hui people) would work hard on the five pillars of Islam: creed, prayer, fasting, almsgiving, and pilgrimage. Wang Mengyang hoped to promote religious teachings to all sectors of society to prevent the ignorant from fabricating stories and confusing right and wrong. Wang Qingyu hoped to accurately survey the Muslim population. The meeting was photographed at 2:00 p.m. and dispersed happily.

Approval from the Executive Yuan 103

The North China Muslim Religious Protection Delegation submitted a petition to the Executive Yuan regarding the case of the South China Literary and Art Magazine insulting the national religion, requesting strict punishment. The approval from the Executive Yuan has now been received, stating that the petition has been received. After investigation, the words insulting Islam written by Lou Zikuang in the first volume, fourteenth issue of the South China Literary and Art Magazine should be investigated and dealt with according to law. The South China Literary and Art Magazine has complied with the central decision and ordered the cessation of publication. As for the editor-in-chief of the magazine, Zeng Zhongming, who published this manuscript, it is difficult to avoid the blame for negligence, but since it has been stated that he did not read it beforehand and has published an apology and voluntarily ceased publication, he should be exempted from discussion. In addition to instructing the Judicial Administration Department to forward the matter to the competent court and have the writer Lou Zikuang promptly dealt with according to law, you are hereby informed of this approval. The Shanghai-Guangdong air route will be postponed.

Shanghai-Tianjin Line Can Be Opened in Spring 104

The Shanghai-Guangzhou air route, which connects Shanghai and Guangzhou, was previously consulted with the China Aviation Corporation. The location and equipment of the airfields along the way have been basically settled. The line could have been test flown in a short period of time and then officially opened to traffic. However, due to obstacles in funding and aircraft, the progress has been slightly slower. Now, the company is focusing on the Shanghai-Tianjin air route. The matter of the Qingdao airfield being occupied by the Japanese is also being handled by the Ministry of Communications, which has consulted with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to send personnel to negotiate with the Japanese side together with the Qingdao Municipal Government. The matter is expected to be resolved soon. Therefore, the company has no time to attend to this Shanghai-Guangzhou air route and will postpone it. However, the Shanghai-Tianjin line can be officially flown in the spring.

A Cemetery for Unknown Heroes Will Be Built in Miaohang

Survey and Construction Began Yesterday, and Roads Will Be Opened at the Same Time 106

People from all walks of life in Shanghai believe that the January 28 Incident was a manifestation of the spirit of our nation. The place where resistance lasted the longest, the shelling was the fiercest, and the casualties were the highest was the Miaohang area. A cemetery for unknown heroes will be built there, and roads will be built to connect Dachang to the west and Lingnan Road in Zhabei to the south. The Jiangsu Province War Zone Relief Committee's Baoshan Branch has been entrusted to handle everything. It is now learned that Shi Wenran and Pan Mengqiao of the branch, together with Wan Kaijia, Director of the Baoshan County Construction Bureau, Lu Qingfeng, Director of the Baoshan County Transportation Affairs Office, and Lu Fengpu, District Chief of the Second District of Baoshan County, went to survey the site at 9:00 a.m. yesterday (the 14th) and construction will begin immediately.

Overseas Chinese National Salvation Association in Burma Advocates Sanctions Against Warlords Who Engage in Civil War 107

The General Association of the Abolish Civil War Alliance received a letter from the Bassein branch of the Overseas Chinese National Salvation Association in Burma, which reads: "In reply to your letter of October 1, and an application for membership, we respectfully learn of your hard work for the country and your new achievements. We are very happy to hear of the official establishment of this General Association. We believe that the biggest reason for the country's peril and the people's livelihood being in decline is the struggle for power and profit by warlords and bureaucrats, and the endless civil wars. The recent war between Han and Liu in Shandong and the wars between various generals in Sichuan are truly infuriating. Now that the lost territories in the Northeast have not yet been recovered, Rehe is under alarm, and Tianjin and Beijing are in danger, we have no time to resist foreign insults and save the country. Yet these warlords are fighting among themselves, harming each other like beans and stalks, with no concept of the nation. Is the flesh of the warlords edible? This General Association was born into this world to awaken the deaf and enlighten the blind, and call out from a high place to alert all directions. We hope that you will work hard to struggle, pool your wisdom and efforts, and work together to turn back the tide. Be sincere and brave, and use it as a pillar in the middle of the stream. For those warlords who are brave in civil war, they should be severely sanctioned. The future of the country may have a chance. A completed application for membership is enclosed with this letter. Please check and accept it. This is to the General Association of the Abolish Civil War Alliance."

Yesterday's Provisional Executive Committee Meeting of the National Association of Lawyers 114

The National Lawyers Association of the Republic of China convened the fourth provisional executive committee meeting at the Shanghai Lawyers Association's office at 3 PM yesterday. Chairman Liu Liumin presided, and Dai Jixian served as recorder. After the meeting began, ㈠ Chairman Liu Liumin reported on the work of this term, then discussed the League of Nations Investigating Committee report. He stated that the facts recorded in the report regarding the responsibility for the incident and the establishment of the puppet state of Manchukuo not being the will of the local people could assert fairness. However, the underlying concept accommodated the established facts, leading to Chapter 10, which absolutely violated the Covenant of the League of Nations, the Nine-Power Treaty, the Pact of Paris, etc. We, for the survival of the Chinese nation and for the sake of peace for all mankind, must resolutely oppose it. Regarding what methods should be adopted to oppose it, please discuss it. After the committee members exchanged opinions, the results of the discussion were: (A) Issue a declaration to the outside world and send it by telegram to the League of Nations in Geneva. At the same time, notify various public organizations within the country with this declaration, asking them to advocate unanimously. The draft will be prepared by committee members such as Li Shirui and Shen Junru, and then reviewed and issued by the association. (B) Send a circular to all lawyers' associations, urging them to initiate donations from their colleagues in a spirit of self-rescue to vigorously assist the Northeast Volunteer Army. Lawyers should also initiate and convene local people's organizations to establish support associations for the Northeast Volunteer Army, and notify all associations of the Shanghai Lawyers Association's fundraising methods for reference.

(C) Proposal for the establishment of the Uniform Legal Rights Movement Committee (resolved) to elect three committee members to be responsible for the organization. Li Shirui, Shen Junru, and Liu Liumin were nominated on the spot to take charge. (D) Whether to restore the association's "Journal of Legal Studies" (resolved) to restore the original publication. The committee members present at today's meeting were nominated to be responsible for carrying out the restoration plan, convened by Committee Member Li Shirui. (E) The Standing Committee proposed to investigate the actual state of the judiciary nationwide. The tasks of the investigation include: ㈠ matters concerning the application of current laws; ㈡ matters concerning the ethics of lawyers and judges; ㈢ matters concerning the facilities of courts, prisons, and detention centers. The investigators will be appointed by the association. For remote provinces, all associations will be entrusted to conduct investigations nearby. (Resolved) To create forms and send them to various lawyers' associations for investigation. If the association deems it necessary, it may send personnel to investigate. (F) The association should request the Ministry of Judicial Administration to issue a circular to all associations, stipulating that in the future, regarding lawyers' applications to inspect case files, extend deadlines, appoint substitute agents, and submit defense statements, judicial paper must comply with the format approved by the Shanghai Lawyers Association in order to standardize and avoid disputes. (Resolved) Passed. (G) Committee Member Dai Tianqiu proposed that lawyers who concurrently serve as executive lawyers in district and county courts should not be restricted to county courts affiliated with local courts. (Resolved) To submit to the Ministry of Judicial Administration for adoption and approval. (H) Committee Member Li Shirui proposed submitting a request to the National Government and the Ministries of Education to instruct all law schools nationwide to add a course on Chinese jurisprudence to their curricula in order to maintain the national legal system. (Resolved) Passed. (I) Discussion of the draft declaration to the outside world. (Resolved) Passed. The meeting adjourned after discussion.

Executive Committee Members Holding Positions in Multiple Associations Cannot Represent Them Simultaneously 120

The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs previously received a submission from the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce regarding whether members of various trade associations who already hold executive committee positions in one industry can be elected as executive committee members in another industry. The bureau requested the municipal government to consult the Ministry of Interior for interpretation. It is now learned that the Ministry of Interior has replied to the municipal government, stating: "Although there are no legal restrictions on one person being elected as an executive committee member of two trade associations, when members of the association attend the Chamber of Commerce as representatives, one person shall not represent two trade associations." It is heard that the municipal government will instruct the Bureau of Social Affairs to forward this reply to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce for reference.

Business tax bureaus in Jing, Rugao, and Tai counties set up checkpoints along the Yangtze River at various ports to intercept and collect pig taxes from passing merchants. The Executive Yuan ordered the Jiangsu Provincial Government to investigate and abolish the tax. It is now heard that the pig tax has been ordered to be abolished and its collection stopped. The Public Utilities Bureau and Other Agencies Rectify Shanghai West Rickshaws

Inspections to be Implemented Starting Today 131

In the four districts of Shanghai West: Fahua, Zhenru, Pusong, and Caojing, unlicensed rickshaws frequently operate for business. These vehicles are mostly old and dilapidated, endangering the safety of travelers and affecting the city's appearance. The Municipal Public Utilities Bureau, Public Security Bureau, and Bureau of Finance had previously discussed rectification measures but suspended them due to the outbreak of the Shanghai Incident. Recently, the bureaus have agreed on four regulatory measures: ㈠ From November 15th to November 30th of this year, will be the inspection period. During this period, all unlicensed rickshaws must apply to the Public Utilities Bureau's Temporary Shanghai West Vehicle Inspection Office (278 Zhongshan Road) for registration and inspection, and classified into the following three grades: (A) Those who pass will be given a temporary operating certificate, allowing them to operate. (B) Those who fail but can be repaired will be instructed to repair the points and issued a re-inspection form, with a deadline for re-inspection. (C) Those who fail and cannot be repaired will be required to make a statement not to operate the original vehicle and return it, and to build a new vehicle for inspection before the end of December of this year. ㈡ Inspections will begin on January 1, 1933. Those without operating certificates will have their vehicles detained and confiscated. ㈢ The scope of the temporary operating certificate is limited to the four districts of Zhenru, Pusong, Caojing, and Fahua. ㈣ Starting in January 1933, the vehicles will pay vehicle tax to the Municipal West Tax Collection Office of the Bureau of Finance based on the temporary operating certificate. The above measures have been presented to the Municipal Government for approval after being jointly submitted by the bureaus and have been announced to the public. Starting today, personnel will be dispatched by the Public

Page 16

Utilities Bureau to be stationed at the Temporary Shanghai West Vehicle Affairs Office opposite the Great Xia University at 278 Zhongshan Road to carry out inspections.

Local Court Burns Confiscated Narcotics 132

The Shanghai Local Court Procuratorate confiscated narcotics and other contraband from the first half of the 21st year. It was scheduled to be burned publicly at 9 AM yesterday, and various agencies were invited to send personnel to supervise. Those who attended included Yu Zonglian, Chief Clerk of the Jiangsu High Court Procuratorate; Lin Woming of the High Second Branch Court; Feng Meixue of the Second Special Court; Ren Bin of the Municipal Party Headquarters; Jin Yuxi of the Command Headquarters; Lu Youchang of the Jianghai Customs; Wu Fengwen of the Municipal Public Security Bureau; and Zhang Xiamen of the County Public Security Bureau. They were received by Court President Shen Xiqing and Prosecutors Cao Changling and Wu Deying and invited to the vacant courtyard in front of the detention center. Deputy Warden Chen Junfang and Police Officer Chen Xihui supervised the court police and servants in unpacking, inspecting, and weighing all the narcotics, which were piled with pine firewood, oil, and salt and set on fire. The burning was completed in the afternoon. The remaining ashes were loaded into burlap bags and thrown into the Huangpu River to eliminate the poisonous atmosphere. A total of 3,815 original sealed items, including opium smoking paraphernalia, were burned, with red blood smoking paraphernalia accounting for the majority.

Good News for the Rectification of Huizhou Tea Industry

Joint Effort by Shanghai and Anhui Institutions 134

The most famous export teas in China are the Wuyuan green tea and Qimen black tea produced in southern Anhui. The total value of China's annual tea exports is approximately 30 million taels, and the Wuyuan and Qimen black and green teas account for almost half of that amount. However, Wuyuan green tea has the disadvantage of being dyed, and its natural fragrance and color are lost. The output of Qimen black tea is small, and the price is surprisingly high, making it difficult to promote. The Construction Department of the Anhui Provincial Government considers tea to be an important product of Anhui Province and plans to improve it. It has reorganized the former National Tea Experiment Station in Qimen into the Provincial Tea Business Station, increasing funding and actively reorganizing it. Recently, it also sent a letter to the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau, requesting the tea inspection director, Wu Juenong, to go to Anhui to plan. It is heard that Mr. Wu has already arrived in Anhui and has formulated detailed plans. He will soon go to the Qimen Tea Station with the technical personnel in Anhui to plan the site and also go to tea-producing areas such as Qiupu, Qimen, Wuyuan, Xiuning, Shexian, and Tunxi to conduct a detailed investigation. In the future, the tea industry in southern Anhui will definitely have considerable development.

Shanghai University Automobile Collides with Tram, Two Killed, Autopsy Conducted 135

On the 12th of this month, a Shanghai University student's car collided with a tram on Yangshupu Road. Student Xu Huandi and passenger Qu Zhengxiang, 16 years old, were both seriously injured. They were taken to Tongren Hospital for treatment. Qu died of his injuries, and Xu died the following morning. This morning, the First Special District Local Court commissioned Prosecutor Zhan Liangce to conduct an autopsy at the autopsy location on Feilun Road. The autopsy confirmed the identities of the corpses. According to Jiang Daifang, 32 years old, who has been driving trams for four years, the car was speeding that day, and he immediately stopped when he saw it, but it was too late. According to the families of the deceased, Xu Huanming and Qu Yan, Prosecutor Zhan obtained the depositions and ruled that the deceased Qu Zhengxiang and Xu Huandi died due to injuries sustained in a collision between the car numbered 16114 and a tram. The bodies were claimed by the families, Qu Yan and Xu Huanming, for coffin preparation. It was found that the driver, Xia Baoquan, is suspected of negligence and should be arrested by the police and interrogated.

Jiangnan Rubber Company Boiler Explosion Injures Four 137

At the Jiangnan Rubber Company, No. 32 Wuhua Road, Yangshupu, yesterday afternoon around 2 PM, while male and female workers were on duty, a boiler (used for melting rubber) in the room suddenly exploded due to excessive heat. Four male and female workers were injured or killed on the spot. They were: male worker Chen Jinfu, 33 years old, from Ningbo, the chief accountant of the factory, who suffered severe abdominal injuries; female worker Zhou Huifen, 18 years old, whose left leg and right arm bones were broken; Ningbo woman Li Chen, 46 years old, whose left arm was broken; and Wuxi woman Min Wu, 32 years old, who died on the spot due to injuries to vital organs. The injured were taken to Tongren Hospital for treatment in a factory vehicle. However, the two women were transferred from that hospital to Guangren Hospital. It is reported that their injuries were so severe that their lives are in danger.

An Old Actor's Impoverished End

Kidnappers Gouge Out His Eyes; Miserable in Old Age, He Hangs Himself 138

Chen Xinghang, 51 years old from Chongqing, used to be a leading actor at the Fujian New Stage, earning over 1,000 yuan per month. He was quite famous, which led to him being targeted by kidnappers. Last winter, on November 16th, he was kidnapped once, and later ransomed for 5,000 yuan. However, when he was about to leave the bandits' den, the bandits, hating his excessive stinginess, gouged out his eyes, rendering him blind. Unable to continue his career, he bought a boat to Shanghai and lived with a friend. Almost a year passed, and as he sat idle, his finances became depleted. Moreover, lacking relatives and friends in Shanghai, he was lonely and miserable. He conceived a desire to die. Yesterday afternoon, he went to the entrance of Ren Zhi Li on Wuchang Road, North Sichuan Road, and hanged himself with his belt. A patrolman spotted him and hired a vehicle to take him to Tongren Hospital for treatment. After a doctor's examination, he was found to be unharmed. The staff at the hospital, pitying his plight, raised funds to buy him a boat ticket and sent someone to accompany him on board, so that he could return safely to his hometown.

Xiong Anshu Commits Suicide After Losing His Job 139

Xiong Anshu, 48 years old from Jiangxi, used to serve in the military. Now unemployed, he was extremely impoverished. The day before yesterday (the 7th), he checked into the Xin Xin Inn in the French Concession. He had been there for over a week, and had pawned almost everything. His livelihood was difficult.
